FACILITY   (LINAC,2ZZZGEL) The 150 MeV Geel electron Linac GELINA,2303900100026 
            giving neutron bursts of 1ns at a rate of 800 Hz. T   2303900100027 
INC-SOURCE (PHOTO) Rotary Uranium Target that is struck by an     2303900100028 
             electron beam with a mean energy of 105 MeV and an   2303900100029 
             average current of 70 microA.                        2303900100030 
INC-SPECT  .White Neutron Source from 2.6 to 20 MeV               2303900100031 
              .EN (keV) - neutron energy(center of the energy bin)2303900100032 
              .EN-RSL-FW (keV) - uncertainty on neutron energy as 2303900100033 
               full width of the energy bin                       2303900100034 
           .The resolution was 8 ns time-of-flight which          2303900100035 
            corresponds to 1.12keV at 1MeV and 35.7keV at 10MeV.  2303900100036 
            The neutron beam was collimated before the fission    2303900100037 
            chamber and its diameter was of 6.1cm+/-0.1cm, less   2303900100038 
            than the diameter of the 235-U deposits and than      2303900100039 
            the diameter of 208-Pb sample.                        2303900100040 
SAMPLE     .Vacuum evaporated deposits, with a total areal density2303900100041 
            of 3.066(6)mg/cm2. The chamber had 5 layers, 3 two-   2303900100042 
            sided and 2 one-sided. The isotopic composition of    2303900100043 
            the Uranium deposits was 99.826(8)% 235-U,            2303900100044 
            0.062(8)% 234-U,0.036(5)% 236-U, and 0.073(9)% 237-U. 2303900100045 
           .Radiogenic 208-Pb metallic sample with a mass of      2303900100046 
            217.45 g, diameter of 69.9 mm +/-0.1 mm and thickness 2303900100047 
            of 5.04 mm. Isotopic content: (88.110+-63)% 208-Pb,   2303900100048 
            (10.988+-64)% 206-Pb, (0.8943+-84)% 207-Pb,           2303900100049 
            (0.00758+-45)% 204-Pb.                                2303900100050 
            The sample diameter was larger than the beam diameter.2303900100051 
METHOD     (TOF) Time-of-flight, with a 198.551m flight path.     2303900100052 
MONITOR    (92-U-235(N,F),,SIG) The neutron flux was measured     2303900100053 
            with a multilayer 235-U fission chamber placed at     2303900100054 
            197.214m flight path.                                 2303900100055

DETECTOR   (HPGE)       The two HPGe detectors and the fission    2303900100106 
            chamber recorded simultaneously. The time resolution  2303900100107 
            of the time coder was 0.5ns. Conventional electronics 2303900100108 
            was used for both HPGe detectors and fission chamber  2303900100109 
            and the Constant Fraction Discriminators of the HPGe  2303900100110 
            detectors were set up on Slow Rise Time Rejection     2303900100111 
            function. The efficiencies were measured with a       2303900100112 
            standard point-like source of 152-Eu of 3.1E+4Bq,     2303900100113 
            using samples of 56-Co and 24-Na produced by neutron  2303900100114 
            activation.                                           2303900100115 
           .4 large volume HPGe detectors, with closed-ended      2303900100116 
            coaxial geometry. The relative efficiencies at 1.33   2303900100117 
            MeV and the distances from the sample position to     2303900100118 
            the detectors were:                                   2303900100119 
             Detector     Angle   Rel.-Efficiency     Distance    2303900100120 
             1            110     75.9%               13.65cm     2303900100121 
             2            150     104.3%              14.65cm     2303900100122 
             3            110     105%                14.2cm      2303900100123 
             4            150     98%                 14.65cm     2303900100124 
             The energy resolution was around 2.4 keV at 1.332MeV.2303900100125 
           (FISCH) The neutron flux was measured with a multilayer2303900100126 
              235-U fission chamber. The fission chamber was used 2303900100127 
            without any change during the measurement campaign    2303900100128 
            that included Cr-52, Bi-209, Pb-208, Pb-207 and Pb-2062303900100129 
            The shape of the neutron flux did not change          2303900100130 
            during this campaign.                                 2303900100131 
ANALYSIS   .The differential gamma production cross-sections at   2303900100132 
            110 and respectively 150 degrees were derived normali-2303900100133 
            sing point by point the HPGe yield to the 235-U       2303900100134 
            fission chamber yield and to the 235U(n,f) cross      2303900100135 
            section.                                              2303900100136 
CORRECTION .The following corrections were done:                  2303900100137 
            1) Correction for the distance between positions of   2303900100138 
               the 208-Pb sample and the position of the fission  2303900100139 
               chamber;                                           2303900100140 
            2) Gamma-ray detection efficiency: extended volume    2303900100141 
               source and self-attenuation of the gamma rays in   2303900100142 
               the 208-Pb sample means of MCNP(version 4c2)       2303900100143 
               simulations. The HPGe efficiencies were corrected  2303900100144 
               for the coincident gamma rays from the 152-Eu      2303900100145 
               source. This correction was about 1%.              2303900100146 
            3) For the angular distribution: Gauss quadrature.    2303900100147 
            4) For multiple scattering and attenuation of the     2303900100148 
               neutron beam in the 208-Pb sample. This was done   2303900100149 
               with MCNP(version 4c2) simulations.                2303900100150 
            5) No acquisition dead time was observed. To avoid    2303900100151 
               the possible dead time introduced in the HPGe      2303900100152 
               detectors acquisition system by the pile-up between2303900100153 
               the neutron induced events and the gamma-flash     2303900100154 
               induced events.                                    2303900100155 
            6) For the isotopic composition of the Pb-208 sample  2303900100156 
            7) The 208Pb(n,2ng) and 208Pb(n,3ng) cross-sections   2303900100157 
               were corrected for the contribution of the (n,xng) 2303900100158 
               reactions on 207-Pb and 206-Pb. The (n,xng) cross  2303900100159 
              sections for 207-Pb and 206-Pb measured during the  2303900100160 
              same campaign. See  L.C.Mihailescu Ph.D. thesis.    2303900100161 
ERR-ANALYS (DATA-ERR) Total uncertainties for the cross sections  2303900100162 
                 were deduced by combining partial uncertainties  2303900100163 
                 from various sources in quadrature. Uncertainty  2303900100164 
                 sources considered were:                         2303900100165 
           (ERR-1,2.3,5.) HPGe efficiencies uncertainties were    2303900100166 
                almost the same for the two detectors, ranging    2303900100167 
                from 2.3% at 0.4MeV up to about 5% at 2.6MeV      2303900100168 
                gamma ray energy.                                 2303900100169 
           (ERR-2) Fission chamber efficiency uncertainty         2303900100170 
                   was 1.62%;                                     2303900100171 
                * 235U(n,f)cross-section uncertainties are point  2303900100172 
                  dependent and are given above together with the 2303900100173 
                  235U(n,f) cross-sections values;                2303900100174 
           (ERR-S,1.4,3.) Statistical counting uncertainties      2303900100175 
               for HPGe detectors and fission chamber are point   2303900100176 
               dependent. The statistical counting uncertainties  2303900100177 
               of the fission chamber yield range from about 1.4% 2303900100178 
               at 2MeV up to about 3% at 18MeV.                   2303900100179

            the above mentioned NIM paper. Together with the list 2303900100181 
            of uncertainties on the quantities in these expres-   2303900100182 
            sions listed above this will allow the evaluator to   2303900100183 
            construct the covariance matrix. See F. Froehner,     2303900100184
